- **Round 1**: The opponent played 'scissors' against my 'scissors'. This suggests either a random choice or a pattern where they repeat their previous play.
- **Round 2**: The opponent played 'rock' against my 'paper'. This could be a random choice or a counter to 'scissors' (if they expected me to repeat my previous play).
- **Round 3**: The opponent played 'paper' against my 'scissors'. This suggests a possible pattern where they might be cycling through 'paper', 'scissors', 'rock', or simply repeating 'paper' after 'rock'.

**Hypothesis Development:**

- The opponent's plays so far ('paper', 'scissors', 'rock', 'paper') could suggest a cyclical pattern: 'paper' -> 'scissors' -> 'rock' -> 'paper'.
- Alternatively, the opponent might be playing a simple adaptive strategy, reacting to my previous plays, but the data is limited to confirm this.
- Given the current data, the hypothesis of a cyclical pattern is plausible, but not definitive.

**Reward Analysis:**

- I received positive rewards when playing 'paper' against 'rock' and 'scissors' against 'paper'.
- I received negative reward when playing 'rock' against 'paper'.
- I received zero reward when playing 'scissors' against 'scissors'.

5. **Conclusion**:

   - This strategy can be exploited by anticipating the next move in the cycle and playing the counter strategy.
